Once walkImport fully\\n611: \\t\\t\\t// plans resources, this case should not longer be needed.\\n612: \\t\\t\\t// In the single instance case, we can return a typed unknown value\\n613: \\t\\t\\t// for the instance to better satisfy other expressions using the\\n614: \\t\\t\\t// value. We\\n619: \\t\\t\\t// don't really have a good value to return otherwise -- empty\\n620: \\t\\t\\t// values will fail for direct index expressions, and unknown\\n621: \\t\\t\\t// Lists and Maps could fail in some type unifications.\\n622: \\t\\t\\tswitch {\\n623: \\t\\t\\tcase config.Count != nil:\\n624: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\\n625: \\t\\t\\tcase config.ForEach != nil:\\n626: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\\n627: \\t\\t\\tdefault:\\n628: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn cty.UnknownVal(ty), diags\\n629: \\t\\t\\t}\\n630: \\n631: \\t\\tdefault:\\n632: \\t\\t\\t// We should only end up here during the validate walk (or\\n633: \\t\\t\\t// console/eval), since later walks should have at least partial\\n634: \\t\\t\\t// states populated for all resources in the configuration.\\n635: \\t\\t\\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\\n636: \\t\\t}\\n637: \\t}\\n638: \\n639: \\t// Now, we're going to build up a value that represents the resource\\n640: \\t// or resources that are in the state.\\n641: \\tinstances := map[addrs.InstanceKey]cty.Value{}\\n642: \\n643: \\t// First, we're going to load any instances that we have written into the\\n644: \\t// deferrals system. A deferred resource overrides anything that might be\\n645: \\t// in the state for the resource, so we do this first.\\n646: \\tfor key, value := range d.Evaluator.Deferrals.GetDeferredResourceInstances(addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath)) {\\n647: \\t\\tinstances[key] = value\\n648: \\t}\\n649: \\n650: \\t// Decode all instances in the current state\\n651: \\tpendingDestroy := d.Operation == walkDestroy\\n652: \\tfor key, is := range rs.Instances {\\n653: \\t\\tif _, ok := instances[key]; ok {\\n654: \\t\\t\\t// Then we've already loaded this instance from the deferrals so\\n655: \\t\\t\\t// we'll just ignore it being in state.\\n656: \\t\\t\\tcontinue\\n657: \\t\\t}\\n658: \\t\\t// Otherwise, we'll load the instance from state.\\n659: \\n660: \\t\\tif is == nil || is.Current == nil {\\n661: \\t\\t\\t// Assume we're dealing with an instance that hasn't been created yet.\\n662: \\t\\t\\tinstances[key] = cty.UnknownVal(ty)\\n663: \\t\\t\\tcontinue\\n664: \\t\\t}\\n665: \\n666: \\t\\tinstAddr := addr.Instance(key).Absolute(d.ModulePath)\\n667: \\t\\tchange := d.Evaluator.Changes.GetResourceInstanceChange(instAddr, addrs.NotDeposed)\\n668: \\t\\tif change != nil {\\n669: \\t\\t\\t// Don't take any resources that are yet to be deleted into account.\\n670: \\t\\t\\t// If the referenced resource is CreateBeforeDestroy, then orphaned\\n671: \\t\\t\\t// instances will be in the state, as they are not destroyed until\\n672: \\t\\t\\t// after their dependants are updated.\\n673: \\t\\t\\tif change.Action == plans.Delete {\\n674: \\t\\t\\t\\tif !pendingDestroy {\\n675: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tcontinue\\n676: \\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n677: \\t\\t\\t}\\n678: \\t\\t}\\n679: \\n680: \\t\\t// Planned resources are temporarily stored in state with empty values,\\n681: \\t\\t// and need to be replaced by the planned value here.\\n682: \\t\\tif is.Current.Status == states.ObjectPlanned {\\n683: \\t\\t\\tif change == nil {\\n684: \\t\\t\\t\\t// FIXME: This is usually an unfortunate case where we need to\\n685: \\t\\t\\t\\t// lookup an individual instance referenced via \\\"self\\\" for\\n686: \\t\\t\\t\\t// postconditions which we know exists, but because evaluation\\n687: \\t\\t\\t\\t// must always get the resource in aggregate some instance\\n688: \\t\\t\\t\\t// changes may not yet be registered.\\n689: \\t\\t\\t\\tinstances[key] = cty.DynamicVal\\n690: \\t\\t\\t\\t// log the problem for debugging, since it may be a legitimate error we can't catch\\n691: \\t\\t\\t\\tlog.Printf(\\\"[WARN] instance %s is marked as having a change pending but that change is not recorded in the plan\\\", instAddr)\\n692: \\t\\t\\t\\tcontinue\\n693: \\t\\t\\t}\\n694: val\\n785: \\t}\\n786: \\n787: \\treturn ret, diags\\n788: }\\n789: \\n790: func (d *evaluationStateData) getEphemeralResource(addr addrs.Resource, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, // Evaluator provides the necessary contextual data for evaluating expressions\n30: // for a particular walk operation.\n31: type Evaluator struct {\n32: \t// Operation defines what type of operation this evaluator is being used\n33: \t// for.\n34: \tOperation walkOperation\n35: \n36: \t// Meta is contextual metadata about the current operation.\n37: \tMeta *ContextMeta\n38: \n39: \t// Config is the root node in the configuration tree.\n40: \tConfig *configs.Config\n41: \n42: \t// Instances tracks the dynamic instances that are associated with each\n43: \t// module call or resource. The graph walk gradually registers the\n44: \t// set of instances for each object within the graph nodes for those\n45: \t// objects, and so as long as the graph has been built correctly the\n46: \t// set of instances for an object should always be available by the time\n47: \t// we're evaluating expressions that refer to it.\n48: \tInstances *instances.Expander\n49: \n50: \t// NamedValues is where we keep the values of already-evaluated input\n51: \t// variables, local values, and output values.\n52: \tNamedValues *namedvals.State\n53: \n54: \t// EphemeralResources tracks the currently-open instances of any ephemeral\n55: \t// resources.\n56: \tEphemeralResources *ephemeral.Resources\n57: \n58: \t// Deferrals tracks resources and modules that have had either their\n59: \t// expansion or their specific planned actions deferred to a future\n60: \t// plan/apply round.\n61: \tDeferrals *deferring.Deferred\n62: \n63: \t// Plugins is the library of available plugin components (providers and\n64: \t// provisioners) that we have available to help us evaluate expressions\n65: \t// that interact with plugin-provided objects.\n66: \t//\n67: \t// From this we only access the schemas of the plugins, and don't otherwise\n68: \t// interact with plugin instances.\n69: \tPlugins *contextPlugins\n70: \n71: \t// State is the current state, embedded in a wrapper that ensures that\n72: \t// it can be safely accessed and modified concurrently.\n73: \tState *states.SyncState\n74: \n75: \t// Changes is the set of proposed changes, embedded in a wrapper that\n76: \t// ensures they can be safely accessed and modified concurrently.\n77: \tChanges *plans.ChangesSync\n78: \n79: \tPlanTimestamp time.Time\n80: }\n81: \n82: // Scope creates an evaluation scope for the given module path and optional\n83: // resource.\n84: //\n85: // If the \"self\" argument is nil then the \"self\" object is not available\n86: // in evaluated expressions. Otherwise, it behaves as an alias for the given\n87: // address.\n88: func (e *Evaluator) Scope(data lang.Data, self addrs.Referenceable, source addrs.Referenceable, extFuncs lang.ExternalFuncs) *lang.Scope {\n89: \treturn &lang.Scope{\n90: \t\tData:          data,\n91: \t\tParseRef:      addrs.ParseRef,\n92: \t\tSelfAddr:      self,\n93: \t\tSourceAddr:    source,\n94: \t\tPureOnly:      e.Operation != walkApply && e.Operation != walkDestroy && e.Operation != walkEval,\n95: \t\tBaseDir:       \".\", // Always current working directory for now.\n96: \t\tPlanTimestamp: e.PlanTimestamp,\n97: \t\tExternalFuncs: extFuncs,\n98: \t}\n99: }\n100: \n101: // evaluationStateData is an implementation of lang.Data that resolves\n102: // references primarily (but not exclusively) using information from a State.\n103: type evaluationStateData struct {\n104: \t*evaluationData\n105: \n106: \t// ModulePath is the path through the dynamic module tree to the module\n107: \t// that references will be resolved relative to.\n108: \tModulePath addrs.ModuleInstance\n109: \n110: \t// InstanceKeyData describes the values, if any, that are accessible due\n111: \t// to repetition of a containing object using \"count\" or \"for_each\"\n112: \t// arguments. *evaluationStateData) GetInputVariable(addr addrs.InputVariable, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n235: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n236: \n237: \t// First we'll make values\n270: \t// rather than for a specific set. Checking against a specific set of\n271: \t// input values then happens during the plan walk.\n272: \t//\n273: \t// This is important because otherwise the validation walk will tend to be\n274: \t// like using input values as\n277: \t// guards to broadly enable/disable resources, avoid processing things\n278: \t// that are disabled, etc. Terraform's static validation leans towards\n279: \t// \t// Output results live in the module that declares them, which is one of\n347: \t// the child module instances of our current module path.\n348: \tmoduleAddr := d.ModulePath.Module().Child(addr.Name)\n349: \tabsAddr := addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath)\n350: \n351: \tparentCfg := d.Evaluator.Config.DescendantForInstance(d.ModulePath)\n352: \tcallConfig, ok := parentCfg.Module.ModuleCalls[addr.Name]\n353: \tif !ok {\n354: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n355: \t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n356: \t\t\tSummary:  `Reference to undeclared \t}\n362: \n363: \t// We'll consult the configuration to see what output names we are\n364: \t// expecting, so we can ensure the resulting object is of the expected\n365: \t// type even if our data is incomplete for some reason.\n366: \tmoduleConfig := d.Evaluator.Config.Descendant(moduleAddr)\n367: \tif moduleConfig == nil {\n368: \t\t// should never happen, since we have a valid module call above, this\n369: \t\t// should be caught during static validation.\n370: \t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"output value read from %s, which has no configuration\", moduleAddr))\n371: \t}\n372: \toutputConfigs := moduleConfig.Module.Outputs\n373: \n374: \t// We don't do instance expansion during validation, and so we need to\n375: \t// return an unknown value. Technically we should always return\n376: \t// cty.DynamicVal here because the final value during plan will always\n377: \t// be an object or tuple type with unpredictable attributes/elements,\n378: \t// but because we never actually carry values forward from validation to\n379: \t// planning we lie a little here and return unknown list and map types,\n380: \t// just to give us more opportunities to catch author mistakes during\n381: \t// validation.\n382: \t//\n383: \t// This means that in practice any expression that refers to a module\n384: \t// call must be written to be valid for either a collection type or\n385: \t// structural type of similar kind, so that it can be considered as\n386: \t// valid during both the validate and plan walks.\n387: \tif d.Operation == walkValidate {\n388: \t\tatys := make(map[string]cty.Type, len(outputConfigs))\n389: \t\tfor name := range outputConfigs {\n390: \t\t\tatys[name] = cty.DynamicPseudoType // output values are dynamically-typed\n391: \t\t}\n392: \t\tinstTy := cty.Object(atys)\n393: \n394: \t\tswitch {\n395: \t\tcase callConfig.Count != nil:\n396: \t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(cty.List(instTy)), diags\n397: \t\tcase callConfig.ForEach != nil:\n398: \t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(cty.Map(instTy)), diags\n399: \t\tdefault:\n400: \t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(instTy), diags\n401: \t\t}\n402: \t}\n403: \n404: \t// For all other walk types, we proceed to dynamic evaluation of individual\n405: \t// instances, using the global instance expander. An earlier graph node\n406: \t// should always have registered the expansion of this module call before\n407: \t// we get here, unless there's a bug in the graph builders.\n408: \tallInstances := d.Evaluator.Instances\n409: \tinstKeyType, instKeys, known := allInstances.ExpandAbsModuleCall(absAddr)\n410: \tif !known {\n411: \t\t// If we don't know which instances exist then we can't really predict\n412: \t\t// anything at all. We can't even predict the return type based on\n413: \t\t// instKeyType because output values are dynamically-typed and so\n414: \t\t// our final result will always be an object or tuple type whose\n415: \t\t// attribute/element count we cannot predict.\n416: \t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n417: \t}\n418: \n419: \tinstanceObjVal := func(instKey addrs.InstanceKey) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n420: \t\t// This function must always return a valid value, even if it's\n421: \t\t// just a cty.DynamicVal placeholder accompanying error diagnostics.\n422: \t\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n423: \n424: \t\tnamedVals := d.Evaluator.NamedValues\n425: \t\tmoduleInstAddr := absAddr.Instance(instKey)\n426: \t\tattrs := make(map[string]cty.Value, len(outputConfigs))\n427: \t\tfor name := range outputConfigs {\n428: \t\t\toutputAddr := moduleInstAddr.OutputValue(name)\n429: \n430: \t\t\t// Although we do typically expect the graph dependencies to\n431: \t\t\t// ensure that values get registered before they are needed,\n432: \t\t\t// we track depedencies with specific output values where\n433: \t\t\t// possible, instead of with entire module calls, and so\n434: \t\t\t// in this specific case it's valid for some of this call's\n435: \t\t\t// output values to not be known yet, with the graph builder\n436: \t\t\t// being responsible for making sure that no expression\n437: \t\t\t// in the configuration can actually observe that.\n438: \t\t\tif !namedVals.HasOutputValue(outputAddr) {\n439: \t\t\t\tattrs[name] = cty.DynamicVal\n440: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n441: \t\t\t}\n442: \t\t\toutputVal := namedVals.GetOutputValue(outputAddr)\n443: \t\t\tattrs[name] = outputVal\n444: \t\t}\n445: \n446: \t\treturn cty.ObjectVal(attrs), diags\n447: \t}\n448: \n449: \tswitch instKeyType {\n450: \n451: \tcase addrs.NoKeyType:\n452: \t\t// In this case we should always have exactly one instance that\n453: \t\t// is addrs.NoKey. If not then there's a bug in the [instances.Expander]\n454: \t\t// implementation.\n455: \t\tif len(instKeys) != 1 {\n456: \t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"module call has no instance key type but has %d instances (should be 1)\", len(instKeys)))\n457: \t\t}\n458: \t\tret, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKeys[0])\n459: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n460: \t\treturn ret, diags\n461: \n462: \tcase addrs.IntKeyType:\n463: \t\t// We can assume that the instance keys are in ascending numerical order\n464: \t\t// and are consecutive, per the contract of allInstances.ExpandModuleCall.\n465: \t\telems := make([]cty.Value, 0, len(instKeys))\n466: \t\tfor _, instKey := range instKeys {\n467: \t\t\tinstVal, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKey)\n468: \t\t\telems = append(elems, instVal)\n469: \t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n470: \t\t}\n471: \t\treturn cty.TupleVal(elems), diags\n472: \n473: \tcase addrs.StringKeyType:\n474: \t\tattrs := make(map[string]cty.Value, len(instKeys))\n475: \t\tfor _, instKey := range instKeys {\n476: \t\t\tinstVal, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKey)\n477: \t\t\tattrs[string(instKey.(addrs.StringKey))] = instVal\n478: \t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n479: \t\t}\n480: \t\treturn cty.ObjectVal(attrs), diags\n481: \n482: \tdefault:\n483: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n484: \t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n485: \t\t\tSummary:  `Unsupported instance key type`,\n486: \t\t\tDetail: fmt.Sprintf(\n487: \t\t\t\t`Module call %s has instance key type %#v, which is not supported by the expression evaluator. This is a bug in Terraform.`,\n488: \t\t\t\tabsAddr, instKeyType,\n489: \t\t\t),\n490: \t\t\tSubject: rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n491: \t\t})\n492: \t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n493: \t}\n494: }\n495: \n496: func (d *evaluationStateData) GetResource(addr addrs.Resource, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n497: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n498: \t// First we'll consult \t}\n518: \n519: \t// Much of this function was written before we had factored out the handling\n520: \t// of instance keys into the separate instance expander model, and so it\n521: \t// does a bunch of instance-related work itself below.\n522: \t//\n523: \t// Currently, unknown instance keys are only possible when planning with\n524: \t// DeferralAllowed set to true in the PlanOpts, which should only be the\n525: \t// case in the stacks runtime (not the \"normal terraform\" modules runtime).\n526: \t// Thus, we have some amount of duplicated code remaining, to be more\n527: \t// certain that stacks-specific behaviors won't leak out into the standard\n528: \t// runtime.\n529: \t//\n530: \t// TODO: When deferred actions are more stable and robust in stacks, it\n531: \t// would be nice to rework this function to rely on the ResourceInstanceKeys\n532: \t// result for _all_ of its work, rather than continuing to duplicate a bunch\n533: \t// of the logic we've tried to encapsulate over ther already.\n534: \tif d.Operation == walkPlan || d.Operation == walkApply {\n535: \t\tif _, _, hasUnknownKeys := d.Evaluator.Instances.ResourceInstanceKeys(addr.Absolute(moduleAddr)); hasUnknownKeys {\n536: \t\t\t// There really isn't anything interesting we can do in this situation,\n537: \t\t\t// because it means we have an unknown for_each/count, in which case\n538: \t\t\t// we here for a single-instance resource because in that\n542: \t\t\t// case we would know that there's only one key and it's addrs.NoKey,\n543: \t\t\t// so we'll fall through to the other logic below.)\n544: \t\t\tunknownVal := cty.DynamicVal\n545: \n546: \t\t\t// If an ephemeral resource is deferred we need to mark the returned unknown value as ephemeral\n547: \t\t\tif addr.Mode == addrs.EphemeralResourceMode {\n548: \t\t\t\tunknownVal = unknownVal.Mark(marks.Ephemeral)\n549: \t\t\t}\n550: \t\t\treturn unknownVal, diags\n551: \t\t}\n552: \t}\n553: \n554: \t// Build the provider address from configuration, since we may not have\n555: \t// state available in all cases.\n556: \t// We need to build an abs provider address, but we can use a default\n557: \t// instance since we're only interested in the schema.\n558: \tschema := d.getResourceSchema(addr, config.Provider)\n559: \tif schema == nil {\n560: \t\t// This shouldn't happen, since validation before we get here the required _root_ module variables are set, which would\\n81: \\t\\t\\t// mask this error with a more specific one that refers to the\\n82: \\t\\t\\t// CLI features for setting such variables. We can get here for\\n83: \\t\\t\\t// child module variables, though.\\n84: \\t\\t\\tlog.Printf(\\\"[ERROR] prepareFinalInputVariableValue: %s is required but is not set\\\", addr)\\n85: \\t\\t\\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\\n86: \\t\\t\\t\\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\\n87: \\t\\t\\t\\tSummary:  `Required variable not set`,\\n88: \\t\\t\\t\\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(`The variable %q is required, but is not set.`, addr.Variable.Name),\\n89: \\t\\t\\t\\tSubject:  cfg.DeclRange.Ptr(),\\n90: \\t\\t\\t})\\n91: \\t\\t\\t// We'll return a placeholder unknown value to avoid producing\\n92: \\t\\t\\t// redundant downstream errors.\\n93: \\t\\t\\treturn cty.UnknownVal(cfg.Type), diags\\n94: \\t\\t}\\n95: \\n96: \\t\\tgiven = defaultVal // must be set, because we checked above that the variable isn't required\\n97: \\t}\\n98: \\n99: \\t// Apply defaults from the variable's type constraint to the converted value,\\n100: \\t// unless the converted value is null. In such a case, the failing secret value should not be\\n128: \\t\\t\\t// displayed to the operator\\n129: \\t\\t\\tif cfg.Sensitive {\\n130: \\t\\t\\t\\tdetail = fmt.Sprintf(\\n131: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\\"The given value is not suitable for %s, which is sensitive: %s. \\n138: \\t\\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\\n139: \\t\\t\\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\\n140: \\t\\t\\tSummary:  \\\"Invalid value for input variable\\\",\\n141: \\t\\t\\tDetail: non-nullable but set to null, and is required\\\", addr)\\n165: \\t\\t\\tif nonFileSource != \\\"\\\" {\\n166: \\t\\t\\t\\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\\n167: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tSeverity: {\\n176: \\t\\t\\t\\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\\n177: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\\n178: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tSummary:  `Required variable not set`,\\n179: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tDetail: ct != 0 {\\n243: \\t\\t\\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\\\"check state says that %s should have no rules, but it has %d\\\", addr, ct))\\n244: \\t\\t}\\n245: \\t\\treturn diags\\n246: \\t}\\n247: \\n248: \\t// We'll build just one evaluation context covering the data needed by\\n249: \\t// all of the rules together, since that'll minimize lock contention\\n250: \\t// on the state, plan, etc.\\n251: \\tscope := ctx.EvaluationScope(nil, nil, EvalDataForNoInstanceKey)\\n252: \\tvar refs []*addrs.Reference\\n253: \\tfor _, rule := range rules {\\n254: \\t\\tcondRefs, moreDiags := langrefs.ReferencesInExpr(addrs.ParseRef, rule.Condition)\\n255: \\t\\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\\n256: \\t\\tmsgRefs, moreDiags := langrefs.ReferencesInExpr(addrs.ParseRef, rule.ErrorMessage)\\n257: \\t\\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\\n258: \\t\\trefs = append(refs, condRefs...)\\n259: \\t\\trefs = append(refs, msgRefs...)\\n260: \\t}\\n261: \\tif diags.HasErrors() {\\n262: \\t\\t// If any of the references were invalid then evaluating the expressions\\n263: \\t\\t// will duplicate those errors, so we'll bail out early.\\n264: \\t\\treturn diags\\n265: \\t}\\n266: \\thclCtx, moreDiags := scope.EvalContext(refs)\\n267: \\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\\n268: \\tif moreDiags.HasErrors() {\\n269: \\t\\treturn diags\\n270: \\t}\\n271: \\n272: \\t// HACK: Historically we manually built a very constrained hcl.EvalContext\\n273: \\t// here, which only included the value of the one specific input variable\\n274: \\t// we're validating, since we didn't yet support referring to anything\\n275: \\t// else. This behaviour did\\n341: \\t// not match that of HCL configuration syntax, where a template\\n342: \\t// expression would result in a validation error.\\n343: \\t//\\n344: \\t// As a result, users writing or generating JSON configuration syntax\\n345: \\t// may have specified error messages which are invalid template\\n346: \\t// expressions. This\\n351: \\t// should only have any effect for JSON configurations. ok {\\n300: \\t\\t\\t// Unfortunately we need to unpack and repack the object here,\\n301: \\t\\t\\t// because cty values are immutable.\\n302: \\t\\t\\tattrs := varsVal.AsValueMap()\\n303: \\t\\t\\tattrs[addr.Variable.Name] = ourVal\\n304: \\t\\t\\thclCtx.Variables[\\\"var\\\"] = cty.ObjectVal(attrs)\\n305: \\t\\t} else {\\n306: \\t\\t\\thclCtx.Variables[\\\"var\\\"] = cty.ObjectVal(map[string]cty.Value{\\n307: \\t\\t\\t\\taddr.Variable.Name: ourVal,\\n308: \\t\\t\\t})\\n309: \\t\\t}\\n310: \\t}\\n311: \\n312: \\tfor ix, validation := range rules {\\n313: \\t\\tresult, ruleDiags := evalVariableValidation(validation, hclCtx, valueRng, addr, ix, validateWalk)\\n314: \\t\\tdiags = diags.Append(ruleDiags)\\n315: \\n316: \\t\\tlog.Printf(\\\"[TRACE] evalVariableValidations: %s status is now %s\\\", addr, result.Status)\\n317: \\t\\tif result.Status == checks.StatusFail {\\n318: \\t\\t\\tcheckState.ReportCheckFailure(addr, addrs.InputValidation, ix, result.FailureMessage)\\n319: \\t\\t} else {\\n320: \\t\\t\\tcheckState.ReportCheckResult(addr, addrs.InputValidation, ix, result.Status)\\n321: \\t\\t}\\n322: \\t}\\n323: \\n324: \\treturn diags\\n325: }\\n326: \\n327: func evalVariableValidation(validation *configs.CheckRule, hclCtx *hcl.EvalContext, valueRng hcl.Range, addr addrs.AbsInputVariableInstance, ix int, validateWalk bool) (checkResult, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\\n328: \\tconst errInvalidCondition = \\\"Invalid variable validation result\\\"\\n329: \\tconst errInvalidValue = \\\"Invalid value for variable\\\"\\n330: \\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\\n331: \\n332: \\tresult, moreDiags := validation.Condition.Value(hclCtx)\\n333: \\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\\n334: \\terrorValue, errorDiags := validation.ErrorMessage.Value(hclCtx)\\n335: \\n336: \\t// The following error handling is a workaround to preserve backwards\\n337: \\t// compatibility. Due to an implementation quirk, all prior versions of\\n338: \\t// Terraform would treat error messages specified using JSON\\n339: \\t// configuration syntax (.tf.json) as string literals, even if they\\n340: \\t// contained the \\\"${\\\" template expression operator. This behaviour did\\n341: \\t// not match that of HCL configuration syntax, where a template\\n342: \\t// expression would result in a validation error.\\n343: \\t//\\n344: \\t// As a result, users writing or generating JSON configuration syntax\\n345: \\t// may have specified error messages which are invalid template\\n346: \\t// expressions. As we add support for error message expressions, we are\\n347: \\t// unable to perfectly distinguish between these two cases.\\n348: \\t//\\n349: \\t// To ensure that we don't break backwards compatibility, we have the\\n350: \\t// below fallback logic if the error message fails to evaluate. This\\n351: \\t// should only have any effect for JSON configurations. The gohcl\\n352: \\t// DecodeExpression function behaves differently when the source of the\\n353: \\t// expression is a JSON configuration file and a nil context is passed.\\n354: \\tif errorDiags.HasErrors() {\\n355: \\t\\t// Attempt to decode the expression as a string literal. We rewrap that as a cty value to allow later\\n363: \\t\\t\\t// decoding to succeed.\\n364: \\t\\t\\terrorValue = cty.StringVal(errorString)\\n365: \\n366: \\t\\t\\t// This warning diagnostic explains this odd behaviour, while\\n367: \\t\\t\\t// giving us an escape hatch to change this to a hard failure\\n368: \\t\\t\\t// in some future Terraform 1.x version.\\n369: \\t\\t\\terrorDiags = hcl.Diagnostics{\\n370: \\t\\t\\t\\t&hcl.Diagnostic{\\n371: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tSeverity:    hcl.DiagWarning,\\n372: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tSummary:     \\\"Validation error message expression is invalid\\\",\\n373: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tDetail:      fmt.Sprintf(\\\"The error message provided could not be evaluated as an expression, so Terraform is interpreting it as a string literal.\\\\n\\\\nIn future versions of Terraform, this will be considered an error. Please file a GitHub issue if this would break your workflow.\\\\n\\\\n%s\\\", errorDiags.Error()),\\n374: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tSubject:     validation.ErrorMessage.Range().Ptr(),\\n375: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tContext:     validation.DeclRange.Ptr(),\\n376: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tExpression:  validation.ErrorMessage,\\n377: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tEvalContext: hclCtx,\\n378: \\t\\t\\t\\t},\\n379: \\t\\t\\t}\\n380: \\t\\t}\\n381: \\n382: \\t\\t// We want to either report the original diagnostics if the\\n383: \\t\\t// fallback failed, or the warning generated above if it succeeded.\\n384: \\t\\tdiags = diags.Append(errorDiags)\\n385: \\t}\\n386: \\n387: \\tif diags.HasErrors() {\\n388: \\t\\tlog.Printf(\\\"[TRACE] evalVariableValidations: %s rule %s check rule evaluation failed: %s\\\", addr, validation.DeclRange, diags.Err().Error())\\n389: \\t}\\n390: \\tif !result.IsKnown() {\\n391: \\t\\tlog.Printf(\\\"[TRACE] evalVariableValidations: %s rule %s condition value is unknown, so skipping validation for now\\\", addr, validation.DeclRange)\\n392: \\n393: \\t\\treturn checkResult{Status: checks.StatusUnknown}, diags // We'll wait until we've learned more, \t\t\t\t\tSubject: sourceRange.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n184: \t\t\t\t})\n185: \t\t\t}\n186: \t\t\t// Stub out our return value so that the semantic checker doesn't\n187: \t\t\t// produce redundant downstream \t\t// module, even if the value assigned to it from outside is not. This\n195: \t\t// is a useful simplification so that module authors can be explicit\n196: \t\t// about what guarantees they are intending to make (regardless of\n197: \t\t// current implementation details). ct != 0 {\n243: \t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"check state says that %s should have no rules, but it has %d\", addr, ct))\n244: \t\t}\n245: \t\treturn diags\n246: \t}\n247: \n248: \t// We'll build just one evaluation context covering the data needed by\n249: \t// all of the rules together, since that'll minimize lock contention\n250: \t// on the state, plan, etc.\n251: \tscope := ctx.EvaluationScope(nil, nil, EvalDataForNoInstanceKey)\n252: \tvar refs []*addrs.Reference\n253: \tfor _, rule := range rules {\n254: \t\tcondRefs, moreDiags := langrefs.ReferencesInExpr(addrs.ParseRef, rule.Condition)\n255: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n256: \t\tmsgRefs, moreDiags := langrefs.ReferencesInExpr(addrs.ParseRef, rule.ErrorMessage)\n257: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n258: \t\trefs = append(refs, condRefs...)\n259: \t\trefs = append(refs, msgRefs...)\n260: \t}\n261: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n262: \t\t// If any of the references were invalid then evaluating the expressions\n263: \t\t// will duplicate those errors, so we'll bail out early.\n264: \t\treturn diags\n265: \t}\n266: \thclCtx, moreDiags := scope.EvalContext(refs)\n267: \tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n268: \tif moreDiags.HasErrors() {\n269: \t\treturn diags\n270: \t}\n271: \n272: \t// HACK: Historically we manually built a very constrained hcl.EvalContext\n273: \t// here, which only included the value of the one specific input variable\n274: \t// we're validating, since we didn't yet support referring to anything\n275: \t// else. Some\\n70: // options in [PlanOpts] when creating a plan must be echoed with equivalent\\n71: // settings during apply, so leaving opts as nil might not be valid for\\n72: // certain combinations of plan-time options.\\n73: func (c *Context) Apply(plan *plans.Plan, config *configs.Config, opts *ApplyOpts) (*states.State, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\\n74: \\tstate, _, diags := c.ApplyAndEval(plan, config, opts)\\n75: \\treturn state, diags\\n76: }\\n77: \\n78: // ApplyAndEval is like [Context.Apply] except that it additionally makes a\\n79: // best effort to return a [lang.Scope] which can evaluate expressions in the\\n80: // root module based on the content of the new state.\\n81: //\\n82: // The scope will be nil if the apply process doesn't complete successfully\\n83: // enough to produce a valid evaluation scope.
